3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
```

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Rust Borrow Checker Error Origin Trace

## Your Task

A Rust user reports `error[E0505]: cannot move out of `x` because it is borrowed`. Trace how this error is generated in the Rust compiler. Find: 1. The Rust source file under `compiler/rustc_borrowck/` that implements the MIR borrow checker and detects move-while-borrowed violations. 2. The file that defines the `BorrowckErrors` or error reporting functions for borrow check diagnostics. 3. The file under `compiler/rustc_borrowck/src/diagnostics/` that formats the E0505 error message. 4. The file under `compiler/rustc_error_codes/src/error_codes/` that defines the `E0505` error code explanation. Report each file path and key function/struct.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the incident domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out. Use Sourcegraph MCP tools to explore the codebase.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/rust--01f6ddf7` (rust-lang/rust)
- `sg-evals/servo--be6a2f99` (servo/servo)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

{"content":"1: A value was moved out while it was still borrowed.\n2: \n3: Erroneous code example:\n4: \n5: ```compile_fail,E0505\n6: struct Value {}\n7: \n8: fn borrow(val: &Value) {}\n9: \n10: fn eat(val: Value) {}\n11: \n12: fn main() {\n13:     let x = Value{};\n14:     let _ref_to_val: &Value = &x;\n15:     eat(x);\n16:     borrow(_ref_to_val);\n17: }\n18: ```\n19: \n20: Here, the function `eat` takes ownership of `x`. However,\n21: `x` cannot be moved because the borrow to `_ref_to_val`\n22: needs to last till the function `borrow`.\n23: To fix that you can do a few different things:\n24: \n25: * Try to avoid moving the variable.\n26: * Release borrow before move.\n27: * Implement the `Copy` trait on the type.\n28: \n29: Examples:\n30: \n31: ```\n32: struct Value {}\n33: \n34: fn borrow(val: &Value) {}\n35: \n36: fn eat(val: &Value) {}\n37: \n38: fn main() {\n39:     let x = Value{};\n40: \n41:     let ref_to_val: &Value = &x;\n42:     eat(&x); // pass by reference, if it's possible\n43:     borrow(ref_to_val);\n44: }\n45: ```\n46: \n47: Or:\n48: \n49: ```\n50: struct Value {}\n51: \n52: fn borrow(val: &Value) {}\n53: \n54: fn eat(val: Value) {}\n55: \n56: fn main() {\n57:     let x = Value{};\n58: \n59:     let ref_to_val: &Value = &x;\n60:     borrow(ref_to_val);\n61:     // ref_to_val is no longer used.\n62:     eat(x);\n63: }\n64: ```\n65: \n66: Or:\n67: \n68: ```\n69: #[derive(Clone, Copy)] // implement Copy trait\n70: struct Value {}\n71: \n72: fn borrow(val: &Value) {}\n73: \n74: fn eat(val: Value) {}\n75: \n76: fn main() {\n77:     let x = Value{};\n78:     let ref_to_val: &Value = &x;\n79:     eat(x); // it will be copied here.\n80:     borrow(ref_to_val);\n81: }\n82: ```\n83: \n84: For more information on Rust's ownership system, take a look at the\n85:

I've successfully traced the Rust compiler's E0505 error generation. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Key Files Found

1. **`compiler/rustc_borrowck/src/lib.rs`** - Contains `mir_borrowck` (entry point) and `check_access_for_conflict` (detection logic)
2. **`compiler/rustc_borrowck/src/diagnostics/conflict_errors.rs`** - Contains `report_move_out_while_borrowed` (generates the error)
3. **`compiler/rustc_borrowck/src/session_diagnostics.rs`** - Defines the `MoveBorrow` diagnostic struct with `code = E0505`
4. **`compiler/rustc_error_codes/src/error_codes/E0505.md`** - Explains the error to users
5. **`compiler/rustc_borrowck/src/borrowck_errors.rs`** - Helper function `cannot_move_when_borrowed`
6. **`compiler/rustc_borrowck/src/diagnostics/move_errors.rs`** - Additional move error handling

## Error Detection Flow

The error is generated through this chain:
1. **`mir_borrowck`** → initiates borrow checking
2. **`check_access_for_conflict`** (line 1246) → detects `WriteKind::Move` on borrowed places
3. **`report_move_out_while_borrowed`** (line 1533) → generates the specific error
4. **`cannot_move_when_borrowed`** → creates the diagnostic struct
5. **`MoveBorrow` struct** → formats and emits E0505

The detailed analysis has been written to `/workspace/answer.json`.

However,\\n21: `x` cannot be moved because the borrow to `_ref_to_val`\\n22: needs to last till the function `borrow`.\\n23: To fix that you can do a few different things:\\n24: \\n25: * Try to avoid moving the variable.\\n26: * Release borrow before move.\\n27: * Implement the `Copy` trait on the type.\\n28: \\n29: Examples:\\n30: \\n31: ```\\n32: struct Value {}\\n33: \\n34: fn borrow(val: &Value) {}\\n35: \\n36: fn eat(val: &Value) {}\\n37: \\n38: fn main() {\\n39:     let x = Value{};\\n40: \\n41:     let ref_to_val: &Value = &x;\\n42:     eat(&x); // pass by reference, if it's possible\\n43:     borrow(ref_to_val);\\n44: }\\n45: ```\\n46: \\n47: Or:\\n48: \\n49: ```\\n50: struct Value {}\\n51: \\n52: fn borrow(val: &Value) {}\\n53: \\n54: fn eat(val: Value) {}\\n55: \\n56: fn main() {\\n57:     let x = Value{};\\n58: \\n59:     let ref_to_val: &Value = &x;\\n60:     borrow(ref_to_val);\\n61:     // ref_to_val is no longer used.\\n62:     eat(x);\\n63: }\\n64: ```\\n65: \\n66: Or:\\n67: \\n68: ```\\n69: #[derive(Clone, Copy)] // implement Copy trait\\n70: struct Value {}\\n71: \\n72: fn borrow(val: &Value) {}\\n73: \\n74: fn eat(val: Value) {}\\n75: \\n76: fn main() {\\n77:     let x = Value{};\\n78:     let ref_to_val: &Value = &x;\\n79:     eat(x); // it will be copied here.\\n80:     borrow(ref_to_val);\\n81: }\\n82: ```\\n83: \\n84: For more information on Rust's ownership system, take a look at the\\n85: [References & Borrowing][references-and-borrowing] section of the Book.\\n86: \\n87: [references-and-borrowing]: https://doc.rust-lang.org/book/ch04-02-references-and-borrowing.html\\n88: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/rust--01f6ddf7@525258043d7f9dcc1b69d9abcb9bfea32826a219/-/blob/compiler/rustc_error_codes/src/error_codes/E0505.md\"}",

    "content": "1: A value was moved out while it was still borrowed.\n2: \n3: Erroneous code example:\n4: \n5: ```compile_fail,E0505\n6: struct Value {}\n7: \n8: fn borrow(val: &Value) {}\n9: \n10: fn eat(val: Value) {}\n11: \n12: fn main() {\n13:     let x = Value{};\n14:     let _ref_to_val: &Value = &x;\n15:     eat(x);\n16:     borrow(_ref_to_val);\n17: }\n18: ```\n19: \n20: Here, the function `eat` takes ownership of `x`. However,\n21: `x` cannot be moved because the borrow to `_ref_to_val`\n22: needs to last till the function `borrow`.\n23: To fix that you can do a few different things:\n24: \n25: * Try to avoid moving the variable.\n26: * Release borrow before move.\n27: * Implement the `Copy` trait on the type.\n28: \n29: Examples:\n30: \n31: ```\n32: struct Value {}\n33: \n34: fn borrow(val: &Value) {}\n35: \n36: fn eat(val: &Value) {}\n37: \n38: fn main() {\n39:     let x = Value{};\n40: \n41:     let ref_to_val: &Value = &x;\n42:     eat(&x); // pass by reference, if it's possible\n43:     borrow(ref_to_val);\n44: }\n45: ```\n46: \n47: Or:\n48: \n49: ```\n50: struct Value {}\n51: \n52: fn borrow(val: &Value) {}\n53: \n54: fn eat(val: Value) {}\n55: \n56: fn main() {\n57:     let x = Value{};\n58: \n59:     let ref_to_val: &Value = &x;\n60:     borrow(ref_to_val);\n61:     // ref_to_val is no longer used.\n62:     eat(x);\n63: }\n64: ```\n65: \n66: Or:\n67: \n68: ```\n69: #[derive(Clone, Copy)] // implement Copy trait\n70: struct Value {}\n71: \n72: fn borrow(val: &Value) {}\n73: \n74: fn eat(val: Value) {}\n75: \n76: fn main() {\n77:     let x = Value{};\n78:     let ref_to_val: &Value = &x;\n79:     eat(x); // it will be copied here.\n80:     borrow(ref_to_val);\n81: }\n82: ```\n83: \n84: For more information on Rust's ownership system, take a look at the\n85: [References & Borrowing][references-and-borrowing] section of the Book.\n86: \n87: [references-and-borrowing]: https://doc.rust-lang.org/book/ch04-02-references-and-borrowing.html\n88: ",
    "url": "https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/rust--01f6ddf7@525258043d7f9dcc1b69d9abcb9bfea32826a219/-/blob/compiler/rustc_error_codes/src/error_codes/E0505.md"
  }
